                              PART 20: TESTING AND QUALITY ASSURANCE                                
                              [Verification Procedures]                                             
                                                                                                    



SECTION 20.1: COMPONENT TESTING CHECKLIST


For each component, verify:

RENDERING:
[ ] Component renders without errors
[ ] No console warnings or errors
[ ] Content displays correctly
[ ] Images load successfully
[ ] Text is readable (contrast, size)

RESPONSIVENESS:
[ ] Mobile (375px) - Layout adapts correctly
[ ] Tablet (768px) - Layout adapts correctly
[ ] Desktop (1024px) - Full layout visible
[ ] Large desktop (1440px+) - No overflow issues

ANIMATIONS:
[ ] Entrance animation triggers correctly
[ ] Hover effects work as expected
[ ] Click/tap effects work
[ ] Scroll-linked animations sync properly
[ ] Exit animations play (if applicable)
[ ] No animation jank or stuttering
[ ] Animations disabled/reduced on mobile where appropriate

INTERACTIONS:
[ ] All buttons/links are clickable
[ ] Forms submit correctly
[ ] Accordions open/close smoothly
[ ] Tabs switch correctly
[ ] Modals open/close properly

ACCESSIBILITY:
[ ] Keyboard navigation works
[ ] Focus states are visible
[ ] Screen reader can navigate content
[ ] Color contrast meets WCAG standards


SECTION 20.2: FULL SITE TESTING PROCEDURE


STEP_BY_STEP_TEST_PROCEDURE:

1. FRESH LOAD TEST
   - Clear browser cache
   - Load site with network throttling (Slow 3G)
   - Verify loading performance
   - Check for layout shifts during load

2. SCROLL TEST
   - Scroll from top to bottom slowly
   - Verify each section animates in
   - Check parallax effects
   - Verify RotatingCard animation (desktop)
   - Ensure no scroll jank

3. NAVIGATION TEST
   - Click menu button
   - Verify overlay animation
   - Click each nav link
   - Verify smooth scroll to sections
   - Verify menu closes after click

4. HOVER TEST (Desktop)
   - Hover over each interactive element
   - Verify cursor preview images appear
   - Check button hover states
   - Verify card hover effects

5. CLICK TEST
   - Click all buttons
   - Click all links
   - Open all accordions
   - Switch all tabs
   - Submit (or validate) any forms

6. MOBILE TEST
   - Use device emulation or real device
   - Verify touch interactions work
   - Check for horizontal scroll issues
   - Verify tap targets are large enough (44px min)
   - Check that complex effects are simplified

7. PERFORMANCE TEST
   - Run Lighthouse audit
   - Check Core Web Vitals
   - Identify and fix any performance issues


SECTION 20.3: PERFORMANCE BENCHMARKS


TARGET_METRICS:

Lighthouse Scores (minimum):
- Performance: 80+
- Accessibility: 90+
- Best Practices: 90+
- SEO: 90+

Core Web Vitals:
- LCP (Largest Contentful Paint): < 2.5s
- FID (First Input Delay): < 100ms
- CLS (Cumulative Layout Shift): < 0.1

Loading:
- First Contentful Paint: < 1.5s
- Time to Interactive: < 3.5s
- Total Bundle Size: < 500KB (gzipped)

Animation:
- Consistent 60fps (no drops below 30fps)
- No visible jank during scroll
- Smooth transitions between states

OPTIMIZATION_TECHNIQUES:

If performance is below targets:

1. Image Optimization:
   - Convert to WebP format
   - Use srcset for responsive images
   - Lazy load below-fold images
   - Compress to reasonable file sizes

2. Code Optimization:
   - Code split large components
   - Lazy load below-fold sections
   - Remove unused dependencies
   - Minify all assets

3. Animation Optimization:
   - Reduce simultaneous animations
   - Use transform instead of layout properties
   - Add will-change sparingly
   - Disable complex effects on mobile

4. Loading Optimization:
   - Preload critical fonts
   - Preconnect to CDNs
   - Inline critical CSS
   - Defer non-critical JavaScript


SECTION 20.4: BROWSER COMPATIBILITY


SUPPORTED_BROWSERS:
- Chrome (latest 2 versions)
- Firefox (latest 2 versions)
- Safari (latest 2 versions)
- Edge (latest 2 versions)
- Mobile Safari (iOS 14+)
- Chrome Mobile (Android 10+)

POTENTIAL_COMPATIBILITY_ISSUES:

1. CSS backdrop-filter:
   - Not fully supported in older Firefox
   - Fallback: Use solid background color

2. CSS scroll-behavior: smooth:
   - Not supported in Safari < 15.4
   - Fallback: JavaScript smooth scroll

3. CSS gap in Flexbox:
   - Not supported in Safari < 14.1
   - Fallback: Use margins

4. CSS aspect-ratio:
   - Not supported in Safari < 15
   - Fallback: Padding-based aspect ratio hack

5. Framer Motion animations:
   - Require JavaScript enabled
   - Provide static fallback for no-JS

TESTING_PROCEDURE:
[ ] Test in Chrome
[ ] Test in Firefox
[ ] Test in Safari (if available)
[ ] Test in Edge
[ ] Test on iOS device/simulator
[ ] Test on Android device/emulator
[ ] Test with JavaScript disabled

║                              PART 21: COMPLETE DEPLOYMENT GUIDE                                    ║
║                              [From Local Development to Production]                                ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

This section provides a complete step-by-step guide for deploying the website to production,
covering Vercel deployment, domain configuration, and post-deployment verification.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 21.1: PRE-DEPLOYMENT CHECKLIST
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Before deploying, verify these items are complete:

CODE_QUALITY_CHECKLIST:
[ ] All TypeScript errors resolved (npm run build passes without errors)
[ ] No console errors visible in browser developer tools
[ ] ESLint warnings addressed (run npm run lint to check)
[ ] Code formatted consistently (npm run format if Prettier is configured)
[ ] All unused imports and variables have been removed from codebase
[ ] Console.log statements removed from production code (use build tools to strip them)
[ ] Dependencies are up to date (run npm outdated to check for updates)
[ ] No security vulnerabilities (run npm audit to identify issues)

CONTENT_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST:
[ ] All placeholder text has been replaced with real client content
[ ] All images are optimized and located in correct public folder locations
[ ] Contact email address has been verified as correct and monitored
[ ] All social media links are valid, active, and point to correct profiles
[ ] Phone number is formatted correctly for international dialing if applicable
[ ] Privacy policy and terms of service pages created if legally required
[ ] All external links have been tested and work correctly
[ ] Copyright year is current and company name is correct

IMAGE_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST:
[ ] All images load correctly when running development server locally
[ ] Image paths are case-sensitive correct (this is critical for Linux servers like Vercel)
[ ] No broken image links exist anywhere on the site
[ ] All images have been optimized and compressed to reasonable file sizes
[ ] WebP format used where browser support is acceptable for major performance gains
[ ] Alt text has been provided for all images for accessibility compliance
[ ] Images are appropriately sized for their containers (no massive images in small spaces)
[ ] Favicon properly displays in browser tab and bookmarks

RESPONSIVE_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST:
[ ] Tested at 375px width (iPhone SE, small mobile)
[ ] Tested at 390px width (iPhone 14 Pro)
[ ] Tested at 768px width (iPad, tablet portrait)
[ ] Tested at 1024px width (iPad landscape, small laptop)
[ ] Tested at 1440px width (standard desktop)
[ ] Tested at 1920px width (large desktop monitor)
[ ] No horizontal scroll issues at any breakpoint
[ ] Touch targets are minimum 44px for mobile accessibility
[ ] Text is readable without zooming at all screen sizes

PERFORMANCE_VERIFICATION_CHECKLIST:
[ ] Lighthouse performance score exceeds 80 (ideally 90+)
[ ] All images below the fold are lazy loaded
[ ] Fonts are preloaded to avoid flash of unstyled text
[ ] Critical CSS is inlined if applicable for faster first paint
[ ] JavaScript bundle is code-split appropriately
[ ] Third-party scripts are loaded asynchronously or deferred

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 21.2: VERCEL DEPLOYMENT PROCESS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

STEP_1_GITHUB_REPOSITORY_SETUP:
Before deploying to Vercel, ensure your code is properly saved in a GitHub repository.
This enables automatic deployments when you push changes.

Here are the exact terminal commands to run:

  # Navigate to your project directory
  cd your-project-folder
  
  # Initialize git repository if not already done
  git init
  
  # Add all project files to git staging
  git add .
  
  # Create initial commit with descriptive message
  git commit -m "Initial commit - complete portfolio website with all sections"
  
  # Add your GitHub repository as remote origin
  git remote add origin https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/YOUR_REPO_NAME.git
  
  # Push to main branch
  git push -u origin main

If you encounter authentication issues, you may need to set up SSH keys or a personal access token.
GitHub has deprecated password authentication for terminal operations.

STEP_2_VERCEL_ACCOUNT_SETUP:
1. Open your web browser and navigate to https://vercel.com
2. Click "Sign Up" if you don't have an account, or "Log In" if you do
3. Select "Continue with GitHub" for the easiest integration
4. Authorize Vercel to access your GitHub repositories when prompted
5. Complete any required profile information

STEP_3_IMPORT_PROJECT_TO_VERCEL:
1. From the Vercel dashboard, click the "Add New..." button
2. Select "Project" from the dropdown menu
3. You'll see a list of your GitHub repositories
4. Find and select the repository containing your portfolio website
5. Vercel will automatically detect that this is a Vite project

STEP_4_CONFIGURE_PROJECT_SETTINGS:
Vercel will auto-detect most settings, but verify these are correct:

  Project Name: your-project-name
    - This becomes part of your URL (your-project-name.vercel.app)
    - Use lowercase letters and hyphens only
    
  Framework Preset: Vite (should be auto-detected)
    - If not detected, select from dropdown
    
  Root Directory: ./
    - Leave as default unless using a monorepo structure
    
  Build Command: npm run build
    - Should be auto-detected from package.json
    - Override if using different build script
    
  Output Directory: dist
    - Vite outputs to dist by default
    - Override if your configuration differs
    
  Install Command: npm install
    - Should be auto-detected
    - Change to yarn install if using Yarn

STEP_5_CONFIGURE_ENVIRONMENT_VARIABLES:
If your project requires environment variables:

1. Click "Environment Variables" section in project settings
2. For each variable, enter the Key and Value
3. Select which environments should have access:
   - Production: Live site only
   - Preview: Branch preview deployments
   - Development: Local development (not commonly used)

Common environment variables for portfolio websites:
  VITE_API_URL         - Backend API endpoint if using one
  VITE_GA_ID           - Google Analytics measurement ID
  VITE_CONTACT_EMAIL   - Contact form destination email
  VITE_SITE_URL        - Canonical URL for SEO purposes

Important: For Vite projects, environment variables must be prefixed with VITE_ to be accessible in client-side code.

STEP_6_DEPLOY_PROJECT:
1. Review all settings are correct
2. Click the "Deploy" button
3. Watch the build logs in real-time for any errors
4. Typical build time is 1-3 minutes for portfolio sites
5. If build fails, review error logs and fix issues

Common build errors and solutions:
  - TypeScript errors: Fix type issues in your code
  - Module not found: Check import paths and file names
  - Image not found: Verify paths and case sensitivity
  - Memory exceeded: Optimize large dependencies

STEP_7_VERIFY_DEPLOYMENT:
Once the build succeeds:

1. Click the preview URL provided by Vercel
2. Your site will open in a new tab
3. Perform these verification checks:
   - Homepage loads without errors
   - All sections are visible and styled correctly
   - Navigation works as expected
   - Images all load properly
   - Animations play smoothly
   - Mobile view works (resize browser or use dev tools)
4. Check browser console for any runtime errors
5. Test on a real mobile device if possible

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 21.3: CUSTOM DOMAIN CONFIGURATION
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

ADDING_CUSTOM_DOMAIN_TO_VERCEL:
To use your own domain name instead of the default .vercel.app subdomain:

1. Go to your project in the Vercel dashboard
2. Click on "Settings" tab at the top
3. Select "Domains" from the left sidebar
4. Type your domain name (e.g., example.com) in the input field
5. Click "Add" button
6. Vercel will check domain ownership and provide DNS instructions

DNS_CONFIGURATION_FOR_YOUR_REGISTRAR:
You'll need to add DNS records at your domain registrar (GoDaddy, Namecheap, Cloudflare, etc.)

For apex domain (example.com - no www):
  Record Type: A
  Host/Name: @ (or leave blank, depending on registrar)
  Value/Points To: 76.76.21.21
  TTL: Auto or 3600 (1 hour)

For www subdomain (www.example.com):
  Record Type: CNAME
  Host/Name: www
  Value/Points To: cname.vercel-dns.com
  TTL: Auto or 3600 (1 hour)

Recommended: Also add a redirect from www to apex (or vice versa) for consistency.
Vercel can configure this automatically in most cases.

DNS_PROPAGATION:
After adding DNS records:
  - Changes can take 1-48 hours to propagate globally
  - Most domains update within 1-4 hours
  - Use a DNS checker tool to verify propagation status
  - Vercel dashboard will show green checkmark when verified

SSL_CERTIFICATE_CONFIGURATION:
Vercel handles SSL certificates automatically:
  - Certificates are issued via Let's Encrypt
  - Automatic provisioning once domain is verified
  - Automatic renewal before expiration
  - HTTPS is enforced by default (HTTP redirects to HTTPS)
  - No manual configuration required

REDIRECT_AND_REWRITE_CONFIGURATION:
For advanced routing needs, create a vercel.json file in your project root:

  {
    "redirects": [
      {
        "source": "/old-page",
        "destination": "/new-page",
        "permanent": true
      },
      {
        "source": "/blog/:slug",
        "destination": "/articles/:slug",
        "permanent": false
      }
    ],
    "headers": [
      {
        "source": "/(.*)",
        "headers": [
          {
            "key": "X-Content-Type-Options",
            "value": "nosniff"
          }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 21.4: CONTINUOUS DEPLOYMENT WORKFLOW
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

AUTOMATIC_DEPLOYMENTS_EXPLAINED:
Once connected to GitHub, Vercel provides automatic deployments:

  Production Deployments:
    - Triggered when you push to the main (or master) branch
    - Deploys to your production domain
    - Previous production deployment becomes available for rollback
    
  Preview Deployments:
    - Triggered when you push to any non-main branch
    - Creates a unique URL for that specific commit
    - Great for testing changes before merging
    
  Pull Request Deployments:
    - Each PR automatically gets a preview deployment
    - Comment on PR includes deployment URL
    - Perfect for code review with visual testing

DEPLOYMENT_WORKFLOW_BEST_PRACTICES:

  1. Development Workflow:
     - Create feature branch from main
     - Make changes and push to feature branch
     - Preview deployment created automatically
     - Test on preview URL
     
  2. Code Review:
     - Open Pull Request on GitHub
     - Share preview deployment URL with reviewers
     - Make revisions based on feedback
     - Each push updates the preview deployment
     
  3. Production Release:
     - Merge PR into main branch
     - Production deployment triggers automatically
     - Verify live site after deployment completes
     - Roll back if issues are discovered

PREVIEW_DEPLOYMENT_FEATURES:
Each preview deployment provides:
  - Unique URL that persists as long as deployment exists
  - Isolated environment from production
  - Same environment variables as production (configurable)
  - Full functionality for testing all features
  - Comments system for feedback (Vercel for Teams)

DEPLOYMENT_PROTECTION_SETTINGS:
For projects requiring additional security:

1. Go to Settings → Deployment Protection
2. Enable Vercel Authentication:
   - Requires Vercel login to view preview deployments
   - Prevents unauthorized access to in-development features
3. Password Protection (Teams/Enterprise):
   - Adds password requirement to view deployments
   - Useful for client review before launch

ROLLBACK_PROCEDURE:
If a deployment causes issues and you need to quickly revert:

1. Go to your project's Deployments tab in Vercel
2. Find the previous working deployment in the list
3. Click the three-dot menu (⋯) next to that deployment
4. Select "Promote to Production"
5. Confirm the promotion
6. Your site immediately reverts to the previous version

This is faster than reverting code changes and redeploying.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 21.5: POST-DEPLOYMENT VERIFICATION
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

COMPREHENSIVE_FUNCTIONALITY_CHECK:
After deployment completes, perform these verification tests:

[ ] Homepage loads correctly without any errors
[ ] All sections scroll smoothly from top to bottom
[ ] Navigation menu opens with proper animation
[ ] Navigation menu closes when clicking outside or on a link
[ ] All navigation links scroll to correct sections
[ ] All external links open in new tabs as expected
[ ] Contact form validates input correctly (if applicable)
[ ] Contact form submits and shows success message (if applicable)
[ ] All animations play correctly and at expected speed
[ ] Hover effects work on interactive elements
[ ] 3D card rotates correctly when scrolling (desktop)
[ ] Gallery horizontal scroll works smoothly
[ ] FAQ accordion items open and close properly
[ ] Filter tabs work in portfolio section
[ ] Mobile menu is accessible and functional

IMAGE_LOADING_CHECK:
Verify all images display correctly:

[ ] Hero section images load and display at correct sizes
[ ] Profile/card images appear without distortion
[ ] Portfolio thumbnail images load for all projects
[ ] Gallery images display without cropping issues
[ ] Service preview images appear on hover
[ ] Social media icons or images load properly
[ ] No placeholder/broken image icons visible anywhere

PERFORMANCE_LIGHTHOUSE_CHECK:
Run Lighthouse audit on your production URL:

1. Open Chrome DevTools (F12 or right-click → Inspect)
2. Go to "Lighthouse" tab
3. Select categories: Performance, Accessibility, Best Practices, SEO
4. Choose "Mobile" or "Desktop" device
5. Click "Analyze page load"
6. Review scores and address any issues

Target scores:
  Performance: > 80 (ideally > 90)
  Accessibility: > 90 (ideally 100)
  Best Practices: > 90 (ideally 100)
  SEO: > 90 (ideally 100)

SEO_VERIFICATION_CHECK:
Verify search engine optimization is properly configured:

[ ] Title tag displays correctly in browser tab
[ ] Meta description is present and accurate
[ ] Open Graph meta tags are configured for social sharing
[ ] Twitter Card meta tags are configured
[ ] Canonical URL is set correctly
[ ] Favicon displays in browser tab and bookmarks
[ ] Site is indexable (check robots.txt allows indexing)
[ ] Sitemap is generated and accessible (if applicable)

ANALYTICS_VERIFICATION_CHECK:
If analytics are configured:

[ ] Google Analytics tracking code is active
[ ] Page views are being recorded (check real-time analytics)
[ ] Custom events are firing correctly (clicks, form submissions)
[ ] Goals and conversions are tracking (if configured)
[ ] User properties are being captured correctly

CROSS_BROWSER_CHECK:
Test your site in multiple browsers:

[ ] Google Chrome (latest version)
[ ] Mozilla Firefox (latest version)
[ ] Safari (latest version, if available)
[ ] Microsoft Edge (latest version)
[ ] Mobile Safari on iOS device
[ ] Chrome on Android device

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                                                                                                    ║
║                              PART 22: ADVANCED ANIMATION TECHNIQUES                                ║
║                              [Complex Motion Patterns and Effects]                                 ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

This section covers advanced animation techniques for creating sophisticated, premium-feeling
interactions that go beyond basic fade and slide effects. These patterns create memorable
user experiences that set professional portfolios apart from basic templates.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 22.1: ORCHESTRATED SEQUENCE ANIMATIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

CONCEPT_OVERVIEW:
Orchestrated animations involve multiple elements animating in a carefully choreographed
sequence. Instead of everything appearing at once, elements reveal themselves in a deliberate
order that guides the user's eye and creates a narrative flow.

KEY_PRINCIPLES:
1. Visual Hierarchy: Most important elements should animate first or most prominently
2. Logical Flow: Animation order should follow natural reading patterns (top-to-bottom, left-to-right)
3. Timing Consistency: Use consistent delays and durations for cohesive feel
4. Completion Awareness: Consider what happens when animation completes

TIMELINE_BASED_SEQUENCE_PATTERN:
This pattern uses Framer Motion variants with stagger to create orchestrated sequences.

The key concepts:
  - Container variant: Controls the overall animation and child orchestration
  - Child variants: Define how each child element animates
  - staggerChildren: Adds delay between each child's animation start
  - delayChildren: Adds initial delay before any children start
  - when: "beforeChildren" ensures container animates before children start

Example implementation:

  const containerVariants = {
    hidden: { 
      opacity: 0 
    },
    visible: {
      opacity: 1,
      transition: {
        when: "beforeChildren",
        staggerChildren: 0.15,
        delayChildren: 0.3
      }
    }
  };

  const titleVariants = {
    hidden: { 
      opacity: 0, 
      y: 30, 
      filter: "blur(10px)" 
    },
    visible: {
      opacity: 1,
      y: 0,
      filter: "blur(0px)",
      transition: {
        duration: 0.8,
        ease: [0.22, 1, 0.36, 1]
      }
    }
  };

  // Additional child variants follow the same pattern
  // Each child can have unique animation properties

WAVE_TEXT_ANIMATION_PATTERN:
Create wave-like effects where characters or words animate in sequence like a wave.
This creates an engaging text reveal that draws attention to important copy.

Implementation approach:
1. Split text into individual characters or words
2. Assign incrementing delays based on position
3. Animate each piece with consistent properties
4. Consider performance for large amounts of text

The visual effect resembles a wave moving through text, with each character
lifting up and settling into place slightly after the previous one.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 22.2: PHYSICS-BASED INTERACTION PATTERNS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

UNDERSTANDING_SPRING_PHYSICS:
Spring animations use physics simulation to create natural-feeling motion.
Unlike duration-based animations, springs feel organic and responsive.

Core spring parameters:
  stiffness: How quickly the spring moves toward target
    - Higher values = faster, snappier motion
    - Lower values = slower, more gradual motion
    - Typical range: 50-500
    
  damping: How quickly oscillation settles
    - Higher values = less bounce, faster settling
    - Lower values = more bounce, longer oscillation
    - Typical range: 10-50
    
  mass: Perceived weight of the animated element
    - Higher values = slower acceleration, more momentum
    - Lower values = faster acceleration, less momentum
    - Typical range: 0.1-3

SPRING_PRESETS_FOR_COMMON_USES:

  Snappy (buttons, toggles):
    stiffness: 500, damping: 30
    
  Responsive (menus, modals):
    stiffness: 300, damping: 25
    
  Smooth (page transitions):
    stiffness: 200, damping: 25
    
  Gentle (decorative elements):
    stiffness: 100, damping: 20
    
  Magnetic (cursor following):
    stiffness: 150, damping: 15, mass: 0.1
    
  Heavy (large elements):
    stiffness: 50, damping: 30, mass: 2

BOUNCE_EFFECT_PATTERN:
Create a bounce animation where an element bounces on click or completion.
This provides satisfying haptic-like feedback for user actions.

The keyframe approach allows precise control over bounce trajectory:
  - Start at rest position (0)
  - Jump up to peak (-20px typically)
  - Return to rest
  - Smaller bounce (-10px)
  - Return to rest
  - Tiny bounce (-5px)
  - Settle at rest

RUBBER_BAND_EFFECT_PATTERN:
Simulate a stretchy, rubber-band effect commonly seen in mobile interfaces.
This effect conveys that an element has been pulled and released.

The animation follows scale changes in X and Y simultaneously:
  - Stretch wider and shorter initially
  - Compress narrower and taller on rebound
  - Multiple oscillations decreasing in intensity
  - Final settle at original scale

JELLY_EFFECT_PATTERN:
Create a wobbly, jelly-like effect on hover or interaction.
This adds playfulness and personality to interface elements.

Key configuration:
  - Low damping for extended wobble
  - Moderate stiffness for quick response
  - Low mass for fast initial reaction

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 22.3: MORPHING AND SHAPE TRANSITIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

BORDER_RADIUS_MORPHING:
Transform elements between different shapes by animating border-radius.
This creates smooth transformations between circles, squares, and rounded rectangles.

Common shape transitions:
  - Circle to square (profile picture hover effects)
  - Rounded rectangle to circle (button states)
  - Organic blob shapes (decorative elements)

Implementation considerations:
  - Use percentage values for responsive scaling
  - Consider width/height changes alongside border-radius
  - Maintain consistent center point during transformation

CLIP_PATH_REVEALS:
Use CSS clip-path with animation for dramatic reveal effects.
Clip-path allows complex shapes beyond simple rectangles.

Common reveal patterns:
  1. Wipe from left: polygon expanding from left edge
  2. Wipe from right: polygon expanding from right edge
  3. Circular reveal: circle expanding from center
  4. Diamond reveal: rotated square expanding from center
  5. Custom shape reveals: defined by specific polygon points

Performance note: clip-path animations are GPU-accelerated and perform well,
but test on lower-powered devices to ensure smoothness.

MASK_BASED_REVEALS:
Similar to clip-path but using CSS masks or gradients.
Useful for softer edges and more complex reveal shapes.

Gradient mask animation:
  - Start with gradient at 0% position
  - Animate gradient to reveal content
  - Can create soft edges unlike clip-path
  - Works well for text reveals

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 22.4: PARALLAX DEPTH LAYERS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

UNDERSTANDING_PARALLAX_DEPTH:
Parallax creates the illusion of depth by moving elements at different speeds.
Elements in the "distance" move slower than elements in the "foreground".

Depth layer hierarchy (back to front):
  1. Background (slowest movement, furthest away)
  2. Mid-ground (moderate movement)
  3. Foreground (fastest movement, closest)
  4. Content (can move opposite direction for effect)

MULTI_LAYER_PARALLAX_IMPLEMENTATION:
Create multiple motion divs, each with different scroll transform rates.

General approach:
  - Use useScroll to track scroll position
  - Apply useTransform to convert scroll to Y position
  - Different output ranges create different speeds
  - Layer with appropriate z-index values

Speed calculation guidelines:
  - Background: 20-30% of scroll distance
  - Mid-ground: 40-60% of scroll distance
  - Foreground: 70-90% of scroll distance
  - Consider viewport height in calculations

MOUSE_PARALLAX_EFFECT:
Similar to scroll parallax but responding to mouse position.
Creates an interactive depth effect as user moves cursor.

Implementation approach:
  - Track mouse position relative to viewport center
  - Apply smaller offset to background elements
  - Apply larger offset to foreground elements
  - Use spring for smooth following motion

COMBINED_SCROLL_AND_MOUSE_PARALLAX:
The most immersive effect combines both scroll and mouse parallax.
Elements respond to both scrolling and cursor movement.

Considerations:
  - Keep movements subtle to avoid motion sickness
  - Reduce or disable on mobile devices
  - Respect prefers-reduced-motion preference
  - Test performance on various devices

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 22.5: GESTURE-BASED ANIMATIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

DRAG_INTERACTION_PATTERNS:
Draggable elements create highly interactive experiences.
Used for sliders, cards, and dismissible elements.

Key properties:
  drag: Enable drag on axis ("x", "y", or true for both)
  dragConstraints: Limit where element can be dragged
  dragElastic: How 'stretchy' the constraints feel (0-1)
  onDragEnd: Callback with velocity and offset data

Visual feedback during drag:
  - Apply rotation based on horizontal movement
  - Scale slightly while being dragged
  - Add shadow to lift element off page
  - Change cursor to grabbing state

SWIPE_GESTURE_PATTERNS:
Swipe gestures are essential for mobile carousel experiences.
Detect swipe direction and velocity to determine action.

Swipe detection approach:
  1. Track drag offset and velocity on drag end
  2. Calculate swipe power (offset × velocity)
  3. Compare against threshold to determine intent
  4. Animate to next/previous item or snap back

Typical swipe threshold: 5000-15000 (adjust based on testing)
Lower threshold = more sensitive swipe detection
Higher threshold = requires more deliberate swipe

PINCH_AND_ZOOM_PATTERNS:
For image galleries and detail views, pinch-to-zoom adds interactivity.

Considerations:
  - Primarily useful on touch devices
  - Requires multi-touch event handling
  - Set minimum and maximum zoom levels
  - Consider pan behavior when zoomed in

COMBINED_GESTURE_STATES:
Many interactive components combine multiple gestures:
  - Drag + tap (draggable cards with click-to-expand)
  - Swipe + long-press (delete actions)
  - Pinch + pan (image viewing)

CASE_STUDY_EXAMPLES:

SECTION 24.1: VERCEL.JSON CONFIGURATION
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

COMPLETE_VERCEL_CONFIG:
Create a `vercel.json` file in the root directory for granular control:

```json
{
  "framework": "nextjs",
  "cleanUrls": true,
  "trailingSlash": false,
  "headers": [
    {
      "source": "/(.*)",
      "headers": [
        {
          "key": "X-Content-Type-Options",
          "value": "nosniff"
        },
        {
          "key": "X-Frame-Options",
          "value": "DENY"
        },
        {
          "key": "X-XSS-Protection",
          "value": "1; mode=block"
        },
        {
          "key": "Referrer-Policy",
          "value": "strict-origin-when-cross-origin"
        }
      ]
    },
    {
      "source": "/images/(.*)",
      "headers": [
        {
          "key": "Cache-Control",
          "value": "public, max-age=31536000, immutable"
        }
      ]
    },
    {
      "source": "/fonts/(.*)",
      "headers": [
        {
          "key": "Cache-Control",
          "value": "public, max-age=31536000, immutable"
        }
      ]
    }
  ],
  "rewrites": [
    {
      "source": "/sitemap.xml",
      "destination": "/api/sitemap"
    }
  ],
  "redirects": [
    {
      "source": "/home",
      "destination": "/",
      "permanent": true
    }
  ],
  "regions": ["sfo1", "iad1"]
}
```

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 24.2: ENVIRONMENT VARIABLES ARCHITECTURE
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

RECOMMENDED_ENV_VARS:
Define these in Vercel Project Settings > Environment Variables:

1. System Configuration:
   NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_URL=https://yourdomain.com
   NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL=https://yourdomain.com/api
   NODE_ENV=production

2. Feature Flags:
   NEXT_PUBLIC_ENABLE_ANALYTICS=true
   NEXT_PUBLIC_ENABLE_BLOG=true
   NEXT_PUBLIC_MAINTENANCE_MODE=false

3. API Keys (Server-side ONLY - no NEXT_PUBLIC prefix):
   EMAIL_SERVER_HOST=smtp.example.com
   EMAIL_SERVER_PORT=587
   EMAIL_SERVER_USER=user@example.com
   EMAIL_SERVER_PASSWORD=secure_password_here
   DATABASE_URL=postgres://user:pass@host:5432/db

4. CMS Integration:
   SANITY_PROJECT_ID=xyz123
   SANITY_DATASET=production
   SANITY_API_TOKEN=secure_token_here

SECURITY_NOTE:
Never commit `.env` files to Git. Add `.env*.local` to `.gitignore`.
Use Vercel's "Encrypted" option for sensitive values like API keys and passwords.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 24.3: ANALYTICS AND MONITORING SETUP
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

VERCEL_ANALYTICS_SETUP:
1. Install dependency: `npm install @vercel/analytics`
2. Add to `_app.tsx` or root layout:
   ```tsx
   import { Analytics } from '@vercel/analytics/react';
   
   export default function App({ Component, pageProps }) {
     return (
       <>
         <Component {...pageProps} />
         <Analytics />
       </>
     );
   }
   ```
3. Enable in Vercel Dashboard > Analytics tab

VERCEL_SPEED_INSIGHTS_SETUP:
1. Install dependency: `npm install @vercel/speed-insights`
2. Add to `_app.tsx` or root layout:
   ```tsx
   import { SpeedInsights } from '@vercel/speed-insights/next';
   
   // ... inside component
   <SpeedInsights />
   ```
3. Enable in Vercel Dashboard > Speed Insights tab

CUSTOM_ERROR_LOGGING (Sentry Integration):
1. `npx sentry-wizard@latest -i nextjs`
2. Follow the wizard to configure project
3. Automatically creates `sentry.client.config.js` and `sentry.server.config.js`
4. Catches unhandled exceptions in production

```javascript
        'slide-up': {

          '100%': { transform: 'translateY(0)', opacity: 1 },
        },
        'fade-in': {
          '0%': { opacity: 0 },
          '100%': { opacity: 1 },
        }
      },

        'gradient-radial': 'radial-gradient(var(--tw-gradient-stops))',
        'mesh': "url('/patterns/mesh.svg')",
```

```css
/* glassmorphism utility */
.glass {
  background: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.05);
  backdrop-filter: blur(10px);
  -webkit-backdrop-filter: blur(10px);
  border: 1px solid rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1);
}

.glass-dark {
  background: rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.4);
  backdrop-filter: blur(12px);
  -webkit-backdrop-filter: blur(12px);
  border: 1px solid rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.05);
}

/* scrollbar hiding */
.no-scrollbar::-webkit-scrollbar {
  display: none;
}
.no-scrollbar {
  -ms-overflow-style: none;
  scrollbar-width: none;
}

/* text gradients */
.text-gradient {
  background-clip: text;
  -webkit-background-clip: text;
  -webkit-text-fill-color: transparent;
  background-image: linear-gradient(to right, var(--color-primary), var(--color-secondary));
}

/* custom selection color */
::selection {
  background: rgba(var(--color-primary), 0.3);
  color: white;
}
```

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗

║                              PART 27: ANIMATION IMPLEMENTATION GUIDE                               ║

╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 27.1: REUSABLE FADE-IN COMPONENT
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

```tsx
/* components/motion/FadeIn.tsx */
import { motion, useInView } from 'framer-motion';
import { useRef } from 'react';

interface FadeInProps {
  children: React.ReactNode;
  delay?: number;
  direction?: 'up' | 'down' | 'left' | 'right' | 'none';
  duration?: number;
  className?: string;
  fullWidth?: boolean;
}

export const FadeIn = ({ 
  children, 
  delay = 0, 
  direction = 'up',
  duration = 0.5,
  className = "",
  fullWidth = false
}: FadeInProps) => {
  const ref = useRef(null);
  const isInView = useInView(ref, { once: true, margin: "-10% 0px" });
  
  const getVariants = () => {
    const distance = 40;
    const variants = {
      hidden: { opacity: 0 },
      visible: { 
        opacity: 1,
        transition: { duration, delay, ease: [0.22, 1, 0.36, 1] }
      }
    };

    if (direction === 'up') variants.hidden['y'] = distance;
    if (direction === 'down') variants.hidden['y'] = -distance;
    if (direction === 'left') variants.hidden['x'] = distance;
    if (direction === 'right') variants.hidden['x'] = -distance;
    
    if (direction !== 'none') {
      variants.visible['y'] = 0;
      variants.visible['x'] = 0;
    }

    return variants;
  };

  return (
    <motion.div
      ref={ref}
      initial="hidden"
      animate={isInView ? "visible" : "hidden"}
      variants={getVariants()}
      className={className}
      style={{ width: fullWidth ? '100%' : 'auto' }}
    >
      {children}
    </motion.div>
  );
};
```

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 27.2: PARALLAX TEXT COMPONENT
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

```tsx
/* components/motion/ParallaxText.tsx */
import { useRef } from "react";
import {
  motion,
  useScroll,
  useSpring,
  useTransform,
  useMotionValue,
  useVelocity,
  useAnimationFrame
} from "framer-motion";
import { wrap } from "@motionone/utils";

interface ParallaxTextProps {
  children: string;
  baseVelocity: number;
}

export function ParallaxText({ children, baseVelocity = 100 }: ParallaxTextProps) {
  const baseX = useMotionValue(0);
  const { scrollY } = useScroll();
  const scrollVelocity = useVelocity(scrollY);
  const smoothVelocity = useSpring(scrollVelocity, {
    damping: 50,
    stiffness: 400
  });
  const velocityFactor = useTransform(smoothVelocity, [0, 1000], [0, 5], {
    clamp: false
  });

  const x = useTransform(baseX, (v) => `${wrap(-20, -45, v)}%`);

  const directionFactor = useRef<number>(1);
  useAnimationFrame((t, delta) => {
    let moveBy = directionFactor.current * baseVelocity * (delta / 1000);

    if (velocityFactor.get() < 0) {
      directionFactor.current = -1;
    } else if (velocityFactor.get() > 0) {
      directionFactor.current = 1;
    }

    moveBy += directionFactor.current * moveBy * velocityFactor.get();

    baseX.set(baseX.get() + moveBy);
  });

  return (
    <div className="parallax">
      <motion.div className="scroller" style={{ x }}>
        <span>{children} </span>
        <span>{children} </span>
        <span>{children} </span>
        <span>{children} </span>
      </motion.div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

Example CSS for above:
```css
.parallax {
  overflow: hidden;
  letter-spacing: -2px;
  line-height: 0.8;
  margin: 0;
  white-space: nowrap;
  display: flex;
  flex-wrap: nowrap;
}

.scroller {
  font-weight: 600;
  text-transform: uppercase;
  font-size: 64px;
  display: flex;
  white-space: nowrap;
  display: flex;
  flex-wrap: nowrap;
}

.scroller span {
  display: block;
  margin-right: 30px;
}
```

Standardized TypeScript interfaces to ensure data consistency across the application.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 28.1: CORE PROJECT TYPES
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

```typescript
/* types/project.ts */

export type ProjectCategory = "Web Design" | "Development" | "Mobile" | "Branding" | "All";

export interface ProjectAuthor {
  name: string;
  role: string;
  avatar: string; // URL
}

export interface ProjectStats {
  value: string;
  label: string;
}

export interface Project {
  id: string;
  slug: string;
  title: string;
  description: string;
  shortDescription: string;
  client: string;
  year: number;
  category: ProjectCategory;
  tags: string[];
  
  // Media
  coverImage: string; // URL
  thumbnailImage: string; // URL
  galleryImages: string[]; // URLs
  
  // Content
  challenge: string;
  solution: string;
  outcome: string;
  stats?: ProjectStats[];
  
  // Tech Stack
  technologies: string[];
  
  // Links
  liveUrl?: string;
  repoUrl?: string;
  
  // Metadata
  isFeatured: boolean;
  publishedAt: string; // ISO Date
}
```

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                                                                                                    ║
║                              PART 24: MICRO-INTERACTION CATALOG                                    ║
║                              [Small Details That Make Big Impressions]                             ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

Micro-interactions are subtle animations that provide feedback, guide users, and add polish
to the user experience. While individually small, collectively they create a feeling of
quality and attention to detail that distinguishes premium websites.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 24.1: BUTTON MICRO-INTERACTIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

RIPPLE_EFFECT:
Material Design-inspired ripple that expands from click point.
Creates satisfying visual feedback confirming the click registered.

Visual behavior:
1. User clicks button at position (x, y)
2. Ripple circle appears at click position
3. Ripple expands outward while fading
4. Ripple completes and removes itself
5. Button action proceeds

Technical considerations:
- Track click position relative to button bounds
- Create animating element at click coordinates
- Remove element after animation completes to prevent memory buildup
- Use transform: scale for performance

ARROW_SLIDE_EFFECT:
Icon animation where arrow slides out and new arrow slides in.
Suggests forward motion and progression.

Visual behavior:
1. Default: Arrow visible at normal position
2. On hover: Arrow slides right and fades out
3. Simultaneously: New arrow slides in from left
4. On hover exit: Reverses the animation

This creates an illusion of continuous forward motion rather than a simple bounce.

LOADING_STATE_TRANSITION:
Smooth transition between default and loading button states.
Maintains button dimensions while communicating action in progress.

Visual behavior:
1. User clicks: Text fades out
2. Loading spinner fades in at center
3. Button opacity reduces slightly
4. On completion: Spinner fades out, text fades in
5. Optionally: Brief success state with checkmark

Animation considerations:
- Use AnimatePresence for exit animations
- Maintain consistent button width to prevent layout shift
- Disable button during loading to prevent double-submission

SUCCESS_STATE_TRANSITION:
After form submission, show success confirmation.

Visual behavior:
1. Loading state completes
2. Success checkmark/icon animates in
3. Button color transitions to success color
4. After brief delay, reverts to default or stays in success state

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 24.2: INPUT FIELD MICRO-INTERACTIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

FLOATING_LABEL:
Label that floats from placeholder position to above input on focus.
Maintains label visibility while allowing full input space.

Visual behavior:
1. Default: Label positioned as placeholder inside input
2. On focus: Label animates up above input border
3. Label scales smaller during animation
4. Label changes color to accent on focus
5. On blur: If empty, label returns to placeholder position
6. If has value: Label stays floating even when unfocused

Animation properties:
- Transform: translateY from 12px to -24px
- Scale: from 1 to 0.85
- Color transition from gray to accent

UNDERLINE_EXPANSION:
Animated underline that expands from center on focus.
Provides clear visual indication of active input.

Visual behavior:
1. Default: No underline visible (or thin gray line)
2. On focus: Accent-colored line animates from center
3. Line expands to full width
4. On blur: Line contracts back to center

Technical implementation:
- Use scaleX with origin-center
- Position absolute at bottom of input
- Height of 2px typically

VALIDATION_FEEDBACK_ANIMATION:
Real-time visual feedback for input validation.

Visual behavior:
1. As user types: Check validation
2. Valid: Green checkmark animates in
3. Invalid: Red X animates in
4. Message appears below with slide-in animation
5. Border color transitions to reflect status

Timing considerations:
- Debounce validation to avoid flickering
- Don't show validation until user has typed
- Clear validation on focus for fresh start

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 24.3: TOGGLE AND SWITCH MICRO-INTERACTIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

ANIMATED_TOGGLE_SWITCH:
Toggle that slides smoothly between on/off states.

Visual behavior:
1. Default off: Knob at left, track dim
2. On toggle: Knob springs to right with bounce
3. Track color transitions to accent
4. Optional: Icon inside knob changes (checkmark/X)
5. Icon transition includes rotation for added flair

Spring configuration:
- Use high stiffness (500) for snappy response
- Moderate damping (30) for slight overshoot
- Quick settling time feels responsive

ICON_MORPHING_TOGGLE:
Toggle where icon morphs between states.

Visual behavior:
1. Off state: X icon
2. During transition: Icon rotates 180°
3. Mid-rotation: Icon cross-fades to checkmark
4. On state: Checkmark visible
5. Reverse on toggle off

This is more engaging than simple icon swap.

COLOR_TRANSITION_TOGGLE:
Track color smoothly interpolates between states.

Technical approach:
- Use animatable background-color
- Or use two overlapping divs with opacity transition
- Ensure transition doesn't feel sluggish

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 24.4: NOTIFICATION MICRO-INTERACTIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

TOAST_NOTIFICATION_ANIMATION:
Notifications that slide in, persist, and slide out.

Entrance animation:
1. Toast appears from right (or bottom)
2. Slides into view with spring animation
3. Brief scale effect on arrival
4. Auto-dismiss timer begins

Exit animation:
1. On dismiss or timeout: Toast slides out
2. Scale reduces slightly during exit
3. Opacity fades to 0
4. Layout animates to fill gap (if stacked)

Stack management:
- Multiple toasts stack vertically
- Use layout animations for smooth reordering
- Limit maximum visible toasts (typically 3-5)

PROGRESS_BAR_IN_TOAST:
Visual timer showing remaining time before auto-dismiss.

Visual behavior:
1. Toast appears with progress bar at 100%
2. Bar animates to 0% over dismiss duration
3. When bar reaches 0%, toast exits
4. If user hovers: Bar pauses
5. On hover exit: Bar resumes from current position

COLOR_CODED_TOAST_TYPES:
Different colors for different message types:
Icon inside toast matches type:
- Success: Checkmark
- Error: X or exclamation

SECTION 34.3: SITEMAP & ROBOTS.TXT
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

DYNAMIC SITEMAP (sitemap.ts):
  export default async function sitemap(): Promise<MetadataRoute.Sitemap> {
    const projects = await getAllProjects();
    
    const projectUrls = projects.map((project) => ({
      url: `https://site.com/projects/${project.slug}`,
      lastModified: new Date(project.updatedAt),
      changeFrequency: 'monthly',
      priority: 0.8,
    }));

    return [
      {
        url: 'https://site.com',
        lastModified: new Date(),
        changeFrequency: 'yearly',
        priority: 1,
      },
      {
        url: 'https://site.com/about',
        lastModified: new Date(),
        changeFrequency: 'monthly',
        priority: 0.8,
      },
      ...projectUrls,
    ];
  }

ROBOTS.TXT (robots.ts):
  export default function robots(): MetadataRoute.Robots {
    return {
      rules: {
        userAgent: '*',
        allow: '/',
        disallow: '/private/',
      },
      sitemap: 'https://site.com/sitemap.xml',
    }
  }

While the portfolio starts static, these patterns allow it to become a dynamic  application
using Supabase for database, auth, and storage.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 35.1: DATABASE SCHEMA DEFINITIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

MESSAGES TABLE (Contact Form):
  create table messages (
    id uuid default uuid_generate_v4() primary key,
    created_at timestamp with time zone default timezone('utc'::text, now()) not null,
    name text not null,
    email text not null,
    message text not null,
    status text default 'unread' check (status in ('unread', 'read', 'archived')),
    ip_address inet
  );

PROJECT_LIKES TABLE (Interactive Feature):
  create table project_likes (
    id uuid default uuid_generate_v4() primary key,
    project_slug text not null,
    session_id text not null,
    created_at timestamp with time zone default now(),
    unique(project_slug, session_id)
  );

ROW LEVEL SECURITY (RLS) POLICIES:
  -- Allow public to insert messages
  create policy "Enable insert for everyone" on messages for insert with check (true);
  
  -- Allow only admin to view messages
  create policy "Enable read for admin" on messages for select using (auth.uid() = 'ADMIN_UUID');

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 35.2: API ROUTE HANDLERS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

HANDLE CONTACT FORM SUBMISSION:
  // app/api/contact/route.ts
  import { createRouteHandlerClient } from '@supabase/auth-helpers-nextjs';
  import { cookies } from 'next/headers';
  import { NextResponse } from 'next/server';

  export async function POST(request: Request) {
    const supabase = createRouteHandlerClient({ cookies });
    const { name, email, message } = await request.json();

    // 1. Validation
    if (!name || !email || !message) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Missing fields' }, { status: 400 });
    }

    // 2. Database Insert
    const { error } = await supabase
      .from('messages')
      .insert({ name, email, message });

    if (error) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: 500 });
    }

    // 3. Optional: Send Email Notification via Resend/SendGrid
    // await sendEmail(...)

    return NextResponse.json({ success: true });
  }

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 35.3: CLIENT-SIDE SUBSCRIPTIONS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

REAL-TIME LIKE COUNTER:
  const [likes, setLikes] = useState(initialLikes);

  useEffect(() => {
    const channel = supabase
      .channel('realtime-likes')
      .on('postgres_changes', {
        event: 'INSERT',
        schema: 'public',
        table: 'project_likes',
        filter: `project_slug=eq.${slug}`
      }, (payload) => {
        setLikes(prev => prev + 1);
      })
      .subscribe();

    return () => {
      supabase.removeChannel(channel);
    }
  }, [slug]);

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗

║                              PART 36: SECURITY BEST PRACTICES & HEADERS                            ║
║                              [Fortifying the Frontend]                                             ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

Security is not an afterthought. These configurations ensure the site is resilient against
common web vulnerabilities like XSS, CSRF, and clickjacking.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 36.1: CONTENT SECURITY POLICY (CSP)
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

STRICT CSP HEADERS (middleware.ts):
  const cspHeader = `
    default-src 'self';
    script-src 'self' 'unsafe-eval' 'unsafe-inline' https://va.vercel-scripts.com https://www.google-analytics.com;
    style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline' https://fonts.googleapis.com;
    img-src 'self' blob: data: https://res.cloudinary.com https://*.google-analytics.com;
    font-src 'self' https://fonts.gstatic.com;
    object-src 'none';
    base-uri 'self';
    form-action 'self';
    frame-ancestors 'none';
    block-all-mixed-content;
    upgrade-insecure-requests;
  `;

  export function middleware(request: NextRequest) {
    const requestHeaders = new Headers(request.headers);
    requestHeaders.set('Content-Security-Policy', cspHeader.replace(/\s{2,}/g, ' ').trim());

    return NextResponse.next({
      headers: requestHeaders,
      request: { headers: requestHeaders },
    });
  }

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 36.2: SECURITY HEADERS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

NEXT.JS CONFIG HEADERS:
  // next.config.js
  module.exports = {
    async headers() {
      return [
        {
          source: '/(.*)',
          headers: [
            {
              key: 'X-DNS-Prefetch-Control',
              value: 'on'
            },
            {
              key: 'Strict-Transport-Security',
              value: 'max-age=63072000; includeSubDomains; preload'
            },
            {
              key: 'X-XSS-Protection',
              value: '1; mode=block'
            },
            {
              key: 'X-Frame-Options',
              value: 'SAMEORIGIN'
            },
            {
              key: 'X-Content-Type-Options',
              value: 'nosniff'
            },
            {
              key: 'Referrer-Policy',
              value: 'origin-when-cross-origin'
            },
            {
              key: 'Permissions-Policy',
              value: 'camera=(), microphone=(), geolocation=(), browsing-topics=()'
            }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  }

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 36.3: INPUT SANITIZATION
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

NEVER trust user input. Use libraries like IDOMPurify or Zod.

ZOD SCHEMA VALIDATION:
  import { z } from 'zod';

  const ContactSchema = z.object({
    name: z.string().min(2, "Name too short").max(50),
    email: z.string().email("Invalid email"),
    message: z.string().min(10, "Message too short").max(1000).transform((val) => {
      // Basic sanitization
      return val.replace(/<[^>]*>/g, '');
    }),
  });

  // Usage in API route
  const result = ContactSchema.safeParse(body);
  if (!result.success) {
    throw new Error(result.error.errors[0].message);
  }

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 37.1: GOOGLE ANALYTICS 4 (GA4) SETUP
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

COMPONENT: <GoogleAnalytics />
  // components/analytics/GoogleAnalytics.tsx
  'use client';

  import Script from 'next/script';

  export default function GoogleAnalytics({ GA_MEASUREMENT_ID }: { GA_MEASUREMENT_ID: string }) {
    return (
      <>
        <Script
          strategy="afterInteractive"
          src={`https://www.googletagmanager.com/gtag/js?id=${GA_MEASUREMENT_ID}`}
        />
        <Script
          id="google-analytics"
          strategy="afterInteractive"
          dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{
            __html: `
              window.dataLayer = window.dataLayer || [];
              function gtag(){dataLayer.push(arguments);}
              gtag('js', new Date());
              gtag('config', '${GA_MEASUREMENT_ID}', {
                page_path: window.location.pathname,
              });
            `,
          }}
        />
      </>
    );
  }

CUSTOM EVENTS TRACKING:
  export const sendGAEvent = (eventName, params) => {
    if (typeof window !== 'undefined' && window.gtag) {
      window.gtag('event', eventName, params);
    }
  }

  // Usage:
  // sendGAEvent('download_resume', { category: 'Engagement', label: 'PDF' });

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 37.2: ERROR BOUNDARIES & LOGGING
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

GLOBAL ERROR BOUNDARY:
Critically important for catching crashes without breaking the whole app.

  'use client';
  
  import { useEffect } from 'react';
  
  export default function Error({
    error,
    reset,
  }: {
    error: Error;
    reset: () => void;
  }) {
    useEffect(() => {
      console.error(error);
      // Optional: Log to Sentry
      // Sentry.captureException(error);
    }, [error]);
  
    return (
      <div className="flex flex-col items-center justify-center min-h-screen bg-black text-white">
        <h2 className="text-2xl font-bold mb-4">Something went wrong!</h2>
        <button
          onClick={reset}
          className="bg-green-500 text-black px-6 py-3 rounded-full font-bold hover:bg-green-400"
        >
          Try again
        </button>
      </div>
    );
  }

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗

We integrate Sanity.io for its flexibility and developer experience.

SECTION 38.1: CONTENT SCHEMAS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

PROJECT SCHEMA (sanity/schemas/project.ts):
  export default {
    name: 'project',
    title: 'Project',
    type: 'document',
    fields: [
      {
        name: 'title',
        title: 'Title',
        type: 'string',
        validation: Rule => Rule.required()
      },
      {
        name: 'slug',
        title: 'Slug',
        type: 'slug',
        options: { source: 'title', maxLength: 96 }
      },
      {
        name: 'mainImage',
        title: 'Main image',
        type: 'image',
        options: { hotspot: true }
      },
      {
        name: 'categories',
        title: 'Categories',
        type: 'array',
        of: [{type: 'reference', to: {type: 'category'}}]
      },
      {
        name: 'publishedAt',
        title: 'Published at',
        type: 'datetime'
      },
      {
        name: 'body',
        title: 'Body',
        type: 'blockContent'
      }
    ]
  }

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 38.2: DATA FETCHING (GROQ)
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

GROQ QUERY UTILITY:
  import { createClient } from "next-sanity";

  const client = createClient({
    projectId: "your-project-id",
    dataset: "production",
    apiVersion: "2023-01-01",
    useCdn: false
  });

  export async function getProjects() {
    return client.fetch(`
      *[_type == "project"] | order(publishedAt desc) {
        _id,
        title,
        "slug": slug.current,
        "imageUrl": mainImage.asset->url,
        categories[]->title
      }
    `);
  }

  // Usage in Server Component:
  // const projects = await getProjects();

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 38.3: LIVE PREVIEW
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Setup Sanity Live Preview to see changes in real-time before publishing.
Requires `next-sanity/preview` and `useLiveQuery`.

  // components/PreviewProjects.tsx
  'use client'
  import { useLiveQuery } from 'next-sanity/preview'

  export default function PreviewProjects({ data }) {
    const [projects] = useLiveQuery(data, projectsQuery);
    return <ProjectList projects={projects} />
  }

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                                                                                                    ║
║                              PART 47: THE ULTIMATE TROUBLESHOOTING GUIDE                           ║
║                              [101 Common Errors & Fixes]                                           ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

When things go wrong, CTRL+F here first.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 47.1: BUILD ERRORS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

ERROR 1: "Hydration failed because the initial UI does not match what was rendered on the server."
FIX: Check for invalid HTML nesting (e.g., <p> inside <p>, <div> inside <p>). Ensure dates/timestamps are formatted consistently on server and client.

ERROR 2: "Module not found: Can't resolve..."
FIX: Run `npm install`, delete `node_modules` and `package-lock.json`, then clean install. Check import paths for case sensitivity.

ERROR 3: "Type 'null' is not assignable to type..."
FIX: Enable strict null checks in `tsconfig.json`. Use optional chaining (`?.`) or non-null assertion (`!`) if you are sure.

ERROR 4: "NextRouter was not mounted"
FIX: You are trying to use `useRouter()` outside of a Next.js page or component tree. Wrap your test with a router provider.

ERROR 5: "Window is not defined"
FIX: You are accessing browser-only APIs (`window`, `document`) during server-side rendering. Wrap in `useEffect` or check `if (typeof window !== 'undefined')`.

ERROR 6: "API resolved without sending a response"
FIX: Ensure your API route handles all code paths and returns a response. Don't use `res.send` inside an async callback without awaiting.

ERROR 7: "Image is missing required 'width' property"
FIX: Local images need import. Remote images need strict width/height or `layout="fill"`.

ERROR 8: "Invalid src prop on `next/image`"
FIX: Add the hostname to `images.domains` in `next.config.js`.

ERROR 9: "React.Children.only expected to receive a single React element child"
FIX: `Link` component (in older Next.js versions) usually expects a single child `<a>`.

ERROR 10: "Error: connect ECONNREFUSED 127.0.0.1:5432"
FIX: Database is ensuring not running. Start Docker container or check connection string.

[... List continues for 90 more common errors ...]

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 47.2: RUNTIME ERRORS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

ERROR 11: "Prop `className` did not match"
FIX: Common with styled-components or emotion when SSR class generation differs. Use babel plugin.

ERROR 12: "Objects are not valid as a React child"
FIX: You are trying to render an object directly. Use `JSON.stringify()` or access properties.

ERROR 13: "Maximum update depth exceeded"
FIX: Infinite loop in `useEffect` or a state update triggering a re-render which triggers the same update. Check dependency arrays.

ERROR 14: "Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'map')"
FIX: The array you are trying to map over is undefined. Initialize state with `[]` or use `data?.map()`.

ERROR 15: "Text content does not match server-rendered HTML"
FIX: Browser extensions often inject code. Try Incognito mode. If persists, check for random data generation on render.

║                              [Database Portability]                                                ║

Sample SQL to instantly hydrate a PostgreSQL database with the structure and mock data.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 49.1: SCHEMA DUMP
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

```sql
-- Enable UUID extension
CREATE EXTENSION IF NOT EXISTS "uuid-ossp";

-- Users / Admins
CREATE TABLE users (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),
  email VARCHAR(255) UNIQUE NOT NULL,
  password_hash VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  role VARCHAR(50) DEFAULT 'user',
  created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
);

-- Projects
CREATE TABLE projects (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),
  slug VARCHAR(255) UNIQUE NOT NULL,
  title VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  description TEXT,
  content_markdown TEXT,
  cover_image_url VARCHAR(255),
  published_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE,
  created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
  updated_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
);

-- Categories
CREATE TABLE categories (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),
  name VARCHAR(100) UNIQUE NOT NULL,
  slug VARCHAR(100) UNIQUE NOT NULL
);

-- Project Categories Pivot
CREATE TABLE project_categories (
  project_id UUID REFERENCES projects(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
  category_id UUID REFERENCES categories(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
  PRIMARY KEY (project_id, category_id)
);

-- Testimonials
CREATE TABLE testimonials (
  id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(),
  author_name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  author_title VARCHAR(255),
  company VARCHAR(255),
  quote TEXT NOT NULL,
  avatar_url VARCHAR(255),
  is_featured BOOLEAN DEFAULT false,
  created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
);
```

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 29.1: UI COMPONENT PROPS
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

BUTTON_PROPS:
```typescript
interface ButtonProps extends React.ButtonHTMLAttributes<HTMLButtonElement> {
  variant?: 'primary' | 'secondary' | 'outline' | 'ghost' | 'danger';
  size?: 'sm' | 'md' | 'lg' | 'xl';
  isLoading?: boolean;
  leftIcon?: React.ReactNode;
  rightIcon?: React.ReactNode;
  isFullWidth?: boolean;
  as?: React.ElementType; // specific mapping (a, button, Link)
}
```

CARD_PROPS:
```typescript
interface CardProps {
  children: React.ReactNode;
  className?: string;
  hoverEffect?: 'lift' | 'shine' | 'none';
  bordered?: boolean;
  padding?: 'none' | 'sm' | 'md' | 'lg';
  onClick?: () => void;
}
```

INPUT_PROPS:
```typescript
interface InputProps extends React.InputHTMLAttributes<HTMLInputElement> {
  label?: string;
  error?: string;
  helperText?: string;
  leftIcon?: React.ReactNode;
  rightIcon?: React.ReactNode;
}
```

MODAL_PROPS:
```typescript
interface ModalProps {
  isOpen: boolean;
  onClose: () => void;
  title?: string;
  children: React.ReactNode;
  size?: 'sm' | 'md' | 'lg' | 'xl' | 'full';
  showCloseButton?: boolean;
  closeOnOverlayClick?: boolean;
}
```

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                                                                                                    ║
║                              PART 30: TESTING & QA STRATEGY                                        ║
║                              [Ensuring Reliability]                                                ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 30.1: UNIT TESTING WITH VITEST
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

SETUP_COMMANDS:
`npm install -D vitest @testing-library/react @testing-library/jest-dom jsdom`

SAMPLE_TEST_FILE (components/Button.test.tsx):
```typescript
import { describe, it, expect, vi } from 'vitest';
import { render, screen, fireEvent } from '@testing-library/react';
import Button from './Button';

describe('Button', () => {
  it('renders children correctly', () => {
    render(<Button>Click me</Button>);
    expect(screen.getByText('Click me')).toBeInTheDocument();
  });

  it('calls onClick handler when clicked', () => {
    const handleClick = vi.fn();
    render(<Button onClick={handleClick}>Click me</Button>);
    fireEvent.click(screen.getByText('Click me'));
    expect(handleClick).toHaveBeenCalledTimes(1);
  });

  it('shows loading state correctly', () => {
    render(<Button isLoading>Click me</Button>);
    expect(screen.getByRole('button')).toBeDisabled();
    expect(screen.getByTestId('spinner')).toBeInTheDocument();
  });
});
```

```typescript
import { test, expect } from '@playwright/test';

test('navigation works correctly', async ({ page }) => {
  await page.goto('http://localhost:3000');

  await page.getByRole('link', { name: 'About' }).click();
```

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                                                                                                    ║
║                              PART 31: PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATION                                     ║
║                              [Speed and Efficiency]                                                ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 31.1: CORE WEB VITALS STRATEGIES
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

LCP (Largest Contentful Paint):
- Preload hero images: `<link rel="preload" as="image" href="/hero.webp">`
- Use `priority` prompt on Next.js Image component for above-the-fold images.
- Optimize server response time (TTFB) with edge caching.

CLS (Cumulative Layout Shift):
- Always define width/height for images and video.
- Reserve space for ads or dynamic content with CSS `min-height`.
- Avoid inserting content above existing content without user interaction.

FID/INP (Interaction to Next Paint):
- Minimize main thread work by code-splitting heavy JS.
- Defer non-critical JS (analytics, chat widgets).
- Use `requestIdleCallback` for low-priority tasks.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 31.2: IMAGE OPTIMIZATION CONFIG
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

NEXT_CONFIG_OPTIMIZATION:
```javascript
// next.config.js
module.exports = {
  images: {
    formats: ['image/avif', 'image/webp'],
    deviceSizes: [640, 750, 828, 1080, 1200, 1920, 2048, 3840],
    imageSizes: [16, 32, 48, 64, 96, 128, 256, 384],
    domains: ['cdn.sanity.io', 'res.cloudinary.com'],
    minimumCacheTTL: 60,
  },
}
```

╔══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╗
║                                                                                                    ║
║                              PART 32: ACCESSIBILITY GUIDELINES                                     ║
║                              [Inclusive Design]                                                    ║
║                                                                                                    ║
╚══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════╝

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 32.1: SEMANTIC HTML CHECKLIST
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

- Use `<main>` for primary content.
- Use `<nav>` for navigation menus.
- Use `<header>` and `<footer>` appropriately.
- Use `<button>` for actions, `<a>` for links (navigation).
- Heading hierarchy (h1 -> h2 -> h3) must be logical and sequential.
- Lists (`<ul>`, `<ol>`) used for groups of items.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 32.2: ARIA ATTRIBUTES
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

- `aria-label`: Use for icon-only buttons (e.g., "Close menu").
- `aria-expanded`: For toggles like mobile menus or accordions.
- `aria-controls`: ID of the element controlled by a button.
- `role="alert"`: For live error messages or success tosts.
- `aria-hidden="true"`: For purely decorative icons.

KEYBOARD NAVIGATION:
- Ensure visible focus states for all interactive elements (`focus-visible`).
- No keyboard traps (user must be able to Tab in and out).
- Skip to content link as the first focusable element.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 34.1: META TAG ARCHITECTURE
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Create a reusable `SEOMeta` component:

```tsx
import Head from 'next/head';

interface SEOProps {
  title: string;
  description: string;
  canonical?: string;
  ogImage?: string;
  noIndex?: boolean;
}

export const SEOMeta = ({ title, description, canonical, ogImage, noIndex }: SEOProps) => {
  const siteUrl = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SITE_URL;
  const fullTitle = `${title} | My Portfolio`;
  
  return (
    <Head>
      <title>{fullTitle}</title>
      <meta name="description" content={description} />
      <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
      {noIndex && <meta name="robots" content="noindex, nofollow" />}
      {canonical && <link rel="canonical" href={`${siteUrl}${canonical}`} />}
      
      {/* Open Graph */}
      <meta property="og:title" content={fullTitle} />
      <meta property="og:description" content={description} />
      <meta property="og:type" content="website" />
      {ogImage && <meta property="og:image" content={ogImage} />}
      
      {/* Twitter */}
      <meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image" />
      <meta name="twitter:title" content={fullTitle} />
      <meta name="twitter:description" content={description} />
      {ogImage && <meta name="twitter:image" content={ogImage} />}
    </Head>
  );
};
```

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 35.1: DATABASE SCHEMA
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

SQL setup for a contact form table:
```sql
create table contacts (
  id bigint generated by default as identity primary key,
  created_at timestamp with time zone default timezone('utc'::text, now()) not null,
  name text not null,
  email text not null,
  message text not null,
  status text default 'new' check (status in ('new', 'read', 'archived'))
);

-- Enable Row Level Security (RLS)
alter table contacts enable row level security;

-- Policy: Allow anyone to insert (public form)
create policy "Anyone can insert contacts"
  on contacts for insert
  with check (true);

-- Policy: Only authenticated admins can view
create policy "Admins can view contacts"
  on contacts for select
  using (auth.role() = 'authenticated');
```

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SECTION 35.2: API ROUTE CLICK HANDLER
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Next.js API Route (pages/api/contact.ts):
```typescript
import { createClient } from '@supabase/supabase-js';
import type { NextApiRequest, NextApiResponse } from 'next';

const supabase = createClient(
  process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL!,
  process.env.SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY! // Secure server-side key
);

export default async function handler(req: NextApiRequest, res: NextApiResponse) {
  if (req.method !== 'POST') {
    return res.status(405).json({ message: 'Method not allowed' });
  }

  const { name, email, message } = req.body;

  if (!name || !email || !message) {
    return res.status(400).json({ message: 'Missing fields' });
  }

  const { data, error } = await supabase
    .from('contacts')
    .insert([{ name, email, message }]);

  if (error) {
    return res.status(500).json({ error: error.message });
  }

  return res.status(200).json({ success: true, data });
}
```
